The MCP Bridge replaces all of this with native MCP channel notifications — messages appear directly in Claude's context, responses come back through MCP tools.\n\nThis is Wave 3 — it only ships after the MCP Bridge is stable and proven in production use.\n\nResearch source: `.channels-research.md` section 8 \"What Gets Removed\".\n\n**Wave:** 3 (Cleanup) — ships only after Wave 2 is stable\n**Dev-workflow path:** Full (high blast radius — large removal across multiple files, careful testing needed)\n\n## Requirements\n\n### Remove from `tmux_bridge.py` (\\~300 LOC)\n\n1. Remove `wait_for_signal()` — relay completion detection (replaced by MCP tool flow)\n4. Remove relay-specific parts of `launch_claude()` — the `-p` flag, pipe-pane setup, JSONL fallback\n5. **KEEP:** `send_text()`, `send_key()`, `capture_pane_clean()`, `is_claude_running()`, `respond_to_question()`, `respond_to_plan()` — still used by `/stop`, `/output`, approval keyboard responses\n\n### Remove from `session_monitor.py` (\\~200 LOC)\n\n1. Remove free-text Q&A handler — no longer needed (bridge handles all inbound messages)\n2. Remove relay watcher tasks — no `claude -p` relay to watch\n3.     "description": "## Context\n\nPart of the Finalize Month initiative (HPH-980), Wave 3. Both layout types exist in the same workbook. This was inherited, not designed for automation.\n\nThe Codex review (finding #6) required optimistic concurrency via eTag + If-Match headers to prevent silent overwrites if someone edits the file concurrently.\n\n**Design doc:** `docs/plans/2026-03-11-finalize-month-design.md` — see \"Excel Injection — Sheet Mapping\" section.\n**Spreadsheet URL:** [https://highlandpethospitalil-my.sharepoint.com/:x:/r/personal/bsterrett_highlandpethospital_com/\\_layouts/15/Doc.aspx?sourcedoc=%7B7C153BFC-F881-45E9-BC36-9E22B10CCF59%7D&file=2026%20AEC%20%26%20HPH%20Benchmarks.xlsx](<https://highlandpethospitalil-my.sharepoint.com/:x:/r/personal/bsterrett_highlandpethospital_com/_layouts/15/Doc.aspx?sourcedoc=%7B7C153BFC-F881-45E9-BC36-9E22B10CCF59%7D&file=2026%20AEC%20%26%20HPH%20Benchmarks.xlsx>)\n\n## Requirements\n\n1. **Graph API download with metadata capture:**\n   * Resolve file path to stable item ID: `GET /users/{upn}/drive/root:/Ben's Files/financial playground/2026 AEC & HPH Benchmarks.xlsx`\n   * Capture `eTag` and `id` from response\n   * Download content: `GET /users/{upn}/drive/items/{id}/content`\n   * Store eTag + itemId in finalization_requests row\n2. **Anchor-based cell mapping engine:**\n   * Do NOT hardcode row numbers. The spreadsheet structure may shift if rows are inserted manually.\n   * Find section anchors by scanning column A for known labels: \"January\", \"February\", ..., \"Revenue\", \"Patients\", \"ATC\", etc.\n   * Find the 2026 year column by scanning the header row for \"2026\"\n   * Build a coordinate map: `{ sheet: \"AEC Benchmarks\", section: \"Revenue\", month: \"January\", row: 17, col: \"M\" }`\n   * Store the map as JSON for debugging and auditability\n3. **Sheet-by-sheet injection** (all 10 sheets):\n\n   | Sheet | Layout | 2026 Column | Data Source |\n   | -- | -- | -- | -- |\n   | AEC |\n   | Liquidi | Bank accounts=rows, months=co | Month colu | monthly_metrics (bank_balanc |\n   | SP | Similar to Liquidi | Month colu | Possibly manual — write what we ha |\n4. **Graph API upload with optimistic concurrency:**\n   * `PUT /users/{upn}/drive/items/{id}/content` with `If-Match: {eTag}` header\n   * If 412 Precondition Failed: someone else edited → fail the step, alert, do NOT overwrite\n   * Store new eTag from response in finalization_requests\n5. **ExcelJS for workbook manipulation:**\n   * Preserves formatting, formulas, styles, merged cells, conditional formatting\n   * Only writes to cells that contain data values — never touches formula cells\n   * Handles both `.xlsx` format correctly\n6. **Plug into daemon pipeline** — replace the stub `downloadExcel()`, Sheet 6\n* Injects retention fund entries into Sheet 7\n* Injects VCF data into Sheet 8\n* Injects liquidity/cash data into Sheet 9\n* Handles Sheet 10 (SPLQ) — writes what we have, skips what we don't\n* Preserves ALL existing formatting, formulas, and styles\n* Upload uses If-Match eTag — concurrent edit causes controlled failure, not silent overwrite\n* Validation test: download → inject test data → verify cells → upload (round-trip)\n* Cell map JSON logged for debugging\n\n## Affected Files/Components\n\n**hph-benchmarks repo:**\n\n* `scripts/automation/finalize-excel.ts` — **new** The `xlsx` (SheetJS) library is faster but more lossy. Use ExcelJS.\n* **Anchor detection strategy:** Scan column A of each sheet for known month names (\"January\"...\"December\") and section headers (\"Revenue\", \"Patients Seen\", \"ATC\", \"Accounts Receivable\"). <!-- call_id: tool_Cuv67OVJN4T04kbnUkv38ypD -->
{
  "id": "a57241c0-c1c9-4c13-95a8-0f02ab68f52e",
  "title": "Write-side idempotency for stock-adjustment retries (PRJ-883 follow-up)",
  "description": "## Context\n\nPRJ-883 (correlation-ID for atomic stock-write reconciliation) shipped with a documented scope reduction: the \"confirmed-not-committed timeouts allow clean retry without double-application risk\" half of the original ticket was deferred under a Codex P1 finding. The current implementation can positively confirm that a timed-out write SUCCEEDED (by finding its movement via correlation ID + server-only read + actor-scoped query) but cannot positively confirm that a write FAILED, because the original transaction promise can still commit arbitrarily long after the client gives up.\n\nTo allow operators to retry a timed-out save without risking double-application of the same adjustment, the WRITE side needs idempotency: a movement created with the same `clientCorrelationId` as a previously-attempted write must either be a no-op or surface a clear \"already applied\" error. Currently the write path treats every call as a fresh write, so a retry after a late-landing original would produce two movements.\n\n## Requirements\n\n* Add a uniqueness check to the movements/create Rule predicate: a write whose `clientCorrelationId` already exists for the same `(itemId, actorUid)` must be rejected.\n* Boundary: on `permission-denied` for that specific reason, return a typed result code (e.g. `'already-applied'`) so the UI can surface \"this adjustment was already saved earlier\" without requiring the operator to think about it.\n* UI (rolls-adjust.tsx): in the timeout `inconclusive` branch, when the operator chooses to retry, REUSE the previous correlationId. The retry then either rule-rejects (`already-applied` → original committed; show late-success state) or succeeds (original failed; clean retry).\n\nTwo paths to consider:\n\n* **Path A (correlation-ID-as-write-key):** Rules require correlationId to be unique per (itemId, actorUid). Retries reuse the SAME correlationId — guaranteeing the second write is rejected if the first committed, and committed if the first failed. UI then uses the SAME correlationId on retry. Cleanest semantic. Requires the UI to remember the original correlationId across the timeout-retry loop, and the operator must explicitly retry (not just \"re-enter the value from scratch\").\n* **Path B (item-state-as-idempotency-key):** Rules require post-write `expectedOldMeters` matches current item state, AND `lastMovementId` cross-reference is validated. This is partially in place already (PRJ-787). Retry generates a fresh correlationId; if the original committed, the item's `remainingMeters` will already equal the retry's `newMeters`, and the retry's transaction will fail the `expectedOldMeters` check. This works for the common case but doesn't catch the case where the retry's `expectedOldMeters` is updated to match the new state — at which point the operator IS double-applying intentionally.\n\nPath A is cleaner. Recommend Path A.\n\n## Acceptance Criteria\n\n* movements/create rule rejects writes whose `clientCorrelationId` already exists for `(itemId, actorUid)`.\n* Boundary surfaces `'already-applied'` typed error code on that rejection.\n* `rolls-adjust.tsx` timeout `inconclusive` branch: when operator chooses to retry, the retry reuses the SAME correlationId as the original attempt. If the original committed, the retry rule-rejects with `already-applied` and UI shows the late-success state (same as the reconcile-found path). If the original failed, the retry succeeds normally.\n* Composite Firestore index updated if needed.\n* PRJ-883 acceptance-criteria item \"Confirmed-not-committed timeouts allow clean retry without double-application risk\" is now satisfied via this ticket's mechanism.\n\n## Affected Files/Components\n\n* `firestore.rules` — movements/create predicate (uniqueness check via `exists()` on a sentinel, or via a query — Rules language has limits here; might need a different approach like a `correlationId-claims` sub-collection).\n* `firestore.indexes.json` — possibly a new index.\n* `src/lib/queries/movements.ts` — boundary error-code mapping.\n* `src/routes/rolls-adjust.tsx` — retry path reuses correlationId.\n\n## Dependencies\n\n* Builds on PRJ-883's correlation ID. Should ship before pilot if the \"clean retry\" capability is wanted; can defer to post-pilot otherwise (the conservative inconclusive message is operator-safe, just less ergonomic).\n\n## Technical Notes\n\n* Firestore Security Rules don't support querying directly. Uniqueness via `exists()` requires a deterministic doc ID derived from `(itemId, actorUid, correlationId)` — likely needs a sentinel `correlationId-claims` collection where each write claims a tuple. This is a non-trivial design and worth its own discussion before implementation.\n* Alternative: a Cloud Function trigger that watches /movements writes and reconciles late-landing duplicates. Adds infra dependency we don't currently have.\n* Path A in the Requirements section is the recommended starting point — but the implementation plan for THIS ticket should re-validate the design before committing to it.",

{
  "id": "d06baf64-a626-436f-ba82-5c611ddc4392",
  "title": "Server-authoritative mount-time reads on safety-critical routes (PRJ-883 follow-up)",
  "description": "## Context\n\nPRJ-883 (correlation-ID for atomic stock-write reconciliation, merged 2026-04-26) shipped with one Codex P2 finding deferred under `owner_override`: the timeout-recovery path on `rolls-adjust.tsx` instructs the operator to reload the page when the reconcile is inconclusive, but the route's mount logic uses cache-backed `getItemById()` rather than `getItemByIdFromServer()`. After a manual reload the new mount can repopulate from persistent local cache — especially if the device is offline or Firestore hasn't fully settled the original transaction — so the operator could still see stale on-hand state on the freshly-reloaded page.\n\nThis isn't unique to `rolls-adjust.tsx`. Several routes in the v1 SPA load critical state via cache-backed reads at mount: `item-form.tsx`, `folder.tsx`, `staff.tsx`, etc. The persistent local cache was enabled deliberately (offline-friendly browsing) but it creates a cache-vs-server-truth mismatch on safety-critical surfaces — most acutely on the stock-adjust route, where pre-commit transaction state can persist in cache for several seconds after the original write.\n\n`getItemByIdFromServer` already exists (PRJ-787 R5) for the post-write reconcile path. The pattern is sound. What's missing is using it on mount of safety-critical routes.\n\n## Requirements\n\n* Audit which routes load state that is safety-critical (stock-correctness or audit-attribution affecting). Initial list:\n  * `src/routes/rolls-adjust.tsx` — stock adjustment surface. **Highest priority.** Mount-time read of `RollItem` should be server-authoritative.\n  * `src/routes/item-form.tsx` (edit mode) — editing item metadata. Cache reads here are probably fine; folder/sku changes don't affect stock correctness.\n  * `src/routes/folder.tsx` — browse + counts. Cache is fine.\n  * `src/routes/staff.tsx` — admin operations on staff. Cache is risky here too: a stale cache could let an admin attempt to deactivate a user who's already been deactivated by a concurrent admin in another session, with confusing error states.\n* For each safety-critical route, replace mount-time `getItemById()`/etc with `getItemByIdFromServer()`/etc. Existing `getItemByIdFromServer` pattern (in `src/lib/queries/items.ts`) is the template — caller MUST handle `firestore/unavailable`, no cache fallback by design.\n* For non-safety-critical routes, keep cache-backed reads (offline-friendly UX is the explicit pilot policy).\n* Add a doc comment at each safety-critical route's mount-effect explaining why server-only is required there.\n\n## Acceptance Criteria\n\n* `rolls-adjust.tsx` mount uses `getItemByIdFromServer()` instead of `getItemById()`. Manual reload on the inconclusive recovery path now guarantees a fresh server snapshot of `remainingMeters`.\n* `staff.tsx` mount uses server-authoritative reads for `listActiveStaff`/`listInactiveStaff` (or equivalent helpers added that bypass cache).\n* Other routes audited and either kept on cache (with a comment explaining why) or moved to server (with a comment explaining why).\n* `firestore/unavailable` (offline at mount-time) surfaces a clear \"you appear to be offline; this page needs a server connection\" message — does NOT silent-fall-back to cache.\n* No regression in offline browsing of folder tree (`folder.tsx` stays cache-friendly).\n\n## Affected Files/Components\n\n* `src/lib/queries/items.ts` — likely already has `getItemByIdFromServer` (verify).\n* `src/lib/queries/users.ts` — may need to add `listActiveStaffFromServer` / `listInactiveStaffFromServer` helpers.\n* `src/routes/rolls-adjust.tsx` — primary fix.\n* `src/routes/staff.tsx` — secondary.\n* Other routes: audit and document decision.\n\n## Dependencies\n\n* None blocking. Should ship before pilot if the inconclusive-recovery flow on `rolls-adjust.tsx` is to be operator-trustworthy under offline conditions.\n\n## Technical Notes\n\n* Vite + persistent local cache means mount-time reads are extra suspect on tablets that move in/out of Wi-Fi range. The pilot environment (storeroom) has documented unreliable Wi-Fi.\n* `getItemByIdFromServer()` requires the SDK to round-trip; if offline, it errors with `firestore/unavailable`. Routes need to handle this error visibly (per the project's \"never silent fail\" invariant).\n* Could be implemented as a smaller scoped change: ONLY `rolls-adjust.tsx` first (the route that prompted this ticket). Other routes' cache-vs-server tradeoff can be evaluated separately if they're not safety-critical.\n* Recommend Path A (`rolls-adjust.tsx` only) for v1 pilot. Wider audit can happen as a follow-up after pilot data shows whether the cache-staleness pattern bites in practice.",

   169

   175	
   176	Bad: "HPH-1028: Execute (IMPLEMENT → VERIFY → REVIEW → DELIVER)"
   177	Good: 4 separate tasks, one for each step

   179	Grouped tasks hide individual step skips from the user. If REVIEW is skipped

   191	on the first TaskUpdate that carries `metadata.dw_step`. When `task_progress_enforcement`

   211	### Standard Path
   212	```
   213	Skill(skill="dw-identify") → Skill(skill="dw-branch") → Skill(skill="dw-discover")
   214	→ Skill(skill="dw-plan")
   215	→ Skill(skill="dw-implement") → Skill(skill="dw-scope-check") → Skill(skill="dw-verify")
   216	→ Skill(skill="dw-simplify") → Skill(skill="dw-review") → Skill(skill="dw-deliver")
   217	→ PR created by teammate → Lead: Skill(skill="dw-pr-review") → Skill(skill="dw-finalize")
   218	```
   219	Teammate creates the PR but does NOT run Codex. Lead runs the sole `pr-review` Codex pass.
   220	
   221	PLAN proceeds directly to IMPLEMENT. Codex reviews arrive at REVIEW (mid-impl diff) and PR-REVIEW (merge gate). No plan-time Codex gate. (PRJ-639, v8.15.0 — dropped dw-validate.)
   222	
   223	### Codex Proof Requirements (PRJ-281, PRJ-387)
   224	
   225	Every Codex gate MUST write proof to `.dw-state.json` decisions array:
   226	```json
   227	{ "step": "pr-review", "gate": "codex", "command": "codex review", "verdict": "APPROVE|REQUEST_CHANGES|REJECT", "timestamp": "ISO" }
   228	```
   229	The `require-pr-review.sh` hook checks for this proof on ALL paths.
   230	
   231	### Agent Team Execution (The Only Model)
   232	
   233	**Skill reference:** `~/.claude/skills/dw-agent-team/SKILL.md`
   234	
   235	Teammates run straight-through with Codex gates. Lead validates via Codex after completion, then merges.
   236	
   237	**This includes skill file updates, documentation changes, and AGENTS.md edits — all implementation work is teammate-owned.**
   238	
   239	**How it works:**
   240	1. Lead creates worktrees per ticket for isolation
   241	2. Lead spawns teammates (stagger 30s apart — OAuth race #37520)
   242	3. Teammates run full dw-* skill sequence straight-through (implement, verify, Semgrep/security review, deliver, create PR). For large hook/skill changes (≥200 LOC or ≥4 files), use the narrower-teammate-scope two-spawn pattern documented in `dw-agent-team` skill — Spawn 1: DISCOVER→PLAN→IMPLEMENT; Spawn 2: SCOPE-CHECK→VERIFY→SIMPLIFY→REVIEW→DELIVER→PR.
   243	4. Lead runs sole `codex review --base main` from worktree after teammate completes
   244	5. Lead auto-proceeds on APPROVE, stops on REQUEST_CHANGES/REJECT
   245	6. Lead merges PRs in dependency order, runs FINALIZE
   246	
   247	<CRITICAL>
   248	Every step MUST be invoked via Skill(skill="dw-*"). Do NOT do the step's work
   249	inline and skip the skill invocation. Skills may have been updated since your
   250	last session. Invoking the skill ensures you follow the current version.
   251	
   252	The rationalization "I already know what this step does" is always wrong.
   253	</CRITICAL>
   254	
   255	## 5.5. Endgame Sequence (PRJ-329)
   256	
   257	Applies to ALL Agent Team flows. This is the strict ordered sequence for merge:
   258	
   259	1. Teammate work complete (all 3 gates passed)
   260	2. Lead runs independent `codex review --base main` from **worktree**
   261	3. Lead validates verdict is explicit (not blank/empty)
   262	4. Lead writes decision with `reviewer_role: "lead"`, `head_sha`, `pr_number`
   263	5. State File Handoff: copy `.dw-state.json` from worktree to main repo
   264	6. Mark `pr-review` phase as `completed` — BEFORE merge (hook runs full checks on completed)
   265	7. cd to main repo. Verify with `git rev-parse --show-toplevel`.
   266	8. Remove worktree (frees branch for `--delete-branch`)
   267	9. Merge: `gh pr merge <PR#> --squash --delete-branch`
   268	10. Post-merge verification: `gh pr view <PR#> --json state` confirms `MERGED`
   269	11. Linear update + Telegram notification + state cleanup (auto via hook)
   270	
   271	See `dw-agent-team` skill for full protocol details.
   272	
   273	## 6. State Updates (SINGLE WRITER — orchestrator only)
   274	
   275	Between each skill invocation:
   276	1. Read `.dw-state.json`
   277	2. Set the completed phase's status to `completed` with `completed_at` timestamp
   278	3. If the step produced decisions/verdicts, append to `decisions` array
   279	4. If the step produced durable IDs (PR number, branch name), update `durable_ids`
   280	5. Set `current_phase` to next phase, set its status to `pending`
   281	6. Update `last_updated`
   282	7. Write `.dw-state.json`
   283	
   284	**8. Mark the step's task complete via TaskUpdate (PRJ-480):**
   285	```
   286	TaskUpdate(taskId: "<id>", status: "completed",
   287	           metadata: { dw_step: "<step-name>", dw_progress_status: "completed" })
   288	```
   289	The PostToolUse hook `track-task-update.sh` writes `.task-progress.json` atomically
   290	with a valid `hook_signature`. **Do NOT write `.task-progress.json` directly** —
   291	the merge gate rejects actor-authored progress when `task_progress_enforcement="hook"`.
   292	
   293	For conditional steps (simplify skipped): include `dw_progress_status: "skipped"`
   294	and `dw_skip_reason: "<why>"` in metadata. The hook records `status: "skipped"`
   295	with the reason. The `task_id` is the numeric ID returned by TaskCreate (e.g., "42").
   296	
   297	**Step skills do NOT write to .dw-state.json.** They output their results inline and the orchestrator persists them.
   298	
   299	### State Schema: Key Fields (PRJ-329, PRJ-387)
   300	
   301	Top-level fields:
   302	- `version`: `"8.0"` — hooks version-gate enforcement based on this field. `"7.0"` accepted for backward compat.
   303	- `execution_model`: `"agent_team"` — the only model. Solo removed in v7.
   304	- `codex_level` (optional, PRJ-642): `"full" | "standard" | "lite_plus" | "lite"` — blast-radius classification computed by `_compute_codex_level` in `hooks/gate-helpers.sh`. **Stateless-recompute:** never persisted as load-bearing state; every caller recomputes from the live working tree. Writing to state is audit-only (breadcrumb in skip decision entries, see below). Hooks NEVER read a persisted `codex_level` field for enforcement — they always recompute. This eliminates stale-state deadlocks. Classification rules: `docs/codex-review-redesign-april-2026.md` Proposal 3.
   305	- `codex_level_rationale` (optional, PRJ-642): human-readable explanation of why the helper returned its classification (e.g., "forced full: hooks/ path"). Audit-only, never read by hooks.
   306	- `task_progress_enforcement` (optional, PRJ-480): `"hook"` opts the workflow into HMAC-signed `.task-progress.json` written exclusively by `track-task-update.sh`. When set, `require-pr-review.sh` BLOCKS on missing/invalid `hook_signature`. Absent/empty → legacy actor-written behavior for backward compat with in-flight workflows. Freshly-bootstrapped workflows via `dev-workflow` orchestrator and `dw-agent-team` set this to `"hook"`. Skills MUST call `TaskUpdate(metadata: { dw_step, dw_progress_status, dw_skip_reason })` — the hook writes the file. Actor-written progress is rejected.
   307	- `codex_level_skip_enabled` (optional, PRJ-652): `true` opts the workflow into the docs-only `codex_level=lite` skip pilot. `dw-agent-team` sets this at state bootstrap. When set, `dw-review` and `dw-pr-review` (teammate-only) may record `gate: "skipped"` decisions and mark their phase status `"skipped"` for lite diffs. Absence/false → skip paths are inert. The merge-gate `_check_codex_level_skip` in `require-pr-review.sh` ALSO requires this flag, so hand-editing the phase status without the flag fails closed.
   308	- `codex_rounds_total` (optional, PRJ-643, default 0): aggregate count of Codex invocations across REVIEW + PR-REVIEW phases. Incremented by `_increment_codex_rounds_total` (in `hooks/gate-helpers.sh`) after each codex run via the wrapper or inline skill snippets. Missing field treated as 0 (additive, no migration). Distinct from the PRJ-434 per-step ceiling at `enforce-verified-commit.sh` — both coexist.
   309	- `codex_rounds_cap` (optional, PRJ-643): integer cap derived from `codex_level` via `_compute_codex_rounds_cap` (`full=6`, `standard=4`, `lite_plus=2`, `lite=1`). Seeded lazily on first increment if missing. Hooks/helpers read this field before each Codex invocation via `_check_codex_rounds_cap`. Over-cap + unresolved CRITICAL/HIGH → wrapper blocks with Telegram notification. Over-cap + clean findings → auto-recorded `cap_extended` exception.
   310	
   311	Phase status enum (expanded, PRJ-652):
   312	- `pending | in_progress | completed` — baseline statuses.
   313	- `skipped` — valid for `simplify` (any reason), `review` (codex_level=lite), and `pr-review` (codex_level=lite, teammate-only). All other steps treat `skipped` as missing and block the merge.
   314	
   315	Skip decision entry shape (PRJ-652):
   316	```json
   317	{
   318	  "step": "review",              // or "pr-review"
   319	  "reviewer_role": "teammate",   // lead never skips pr-review
   320	  "gate": "skipped",
   321	  "codex_level": "lite",         // MUST equal "lite" — pilot guardrail
   322	  "head_sha": "<40-char hex>",
   323	  "timestamp": "<ISO8601>",
   324	  "reason": "codex_level=lite: <N> docs file(s), <M> LOC"
   325	}
   326	```
   327	Resume-invalidation marks prior entries `superseded: true` (plus `superseded_at`) rather than deleting them — audit trail preservation.
   328	
   329	Decision entry fields (in `.decisions[]`):
   330	- `reviewer_role`: `"lead"` (orchestrating Claude) or `"teammate"` (implementing Claude)
   331	- `head_sha`: git HEAD SHA at time of review — validated at merge to catch stale approvals.
   332	  The hook checks presence (not empty), the skill captures and validates freshness.
   333	- `repo_context`: absolute path where review was run (audit trail, not enforced in hooks —
   334	  worktree paths differ from main repo)
   335	- `pr_number` in decision entry: redundant with `durable_ids.pr_number` but makes each
   336	  decision self-contained for cross-context validation
   337	
   338	### Finding Status in Decisions (PRJ-300)
   339	
   340	When the REVIEW step reports findings, persist granular status in the decisions array:
   341	
   342	```json
   343	{
   344	  "step": "review",
   345	  "gate": "codex",
   346	  "finding_status": "fix_applied|proof_collected|re_review_passed|merge_eligible",
   347	  "findings_count": 2,
   348	  "findings_fixed": 1,
   349	  "findings_deferred": 1,
   350	  "timestamp": "ISO"
   351	}
   352	```
   353	
   354	**Finding status values:**
   355	- `finding_received` — reviewer identified a defect
   356	- `fix_applied` — code changed to address finding
   357	- `proof_collected` — behavioral proof artifact attached (Finding Resolution block written)
   358	- `re_review_passed` — second review confirms resolution (escalation-class findings only)
   359	- `merge_eligible` — all CRITICAL/HIGH/MEDIUM findings at `proof_collected` or above. Deferred LOW findings (Linear-only) do not block merge eligibility.
   360	
   361	Use the most advanced status reached. If no findings, omit `finding_status` (clean pass).
   362	Escalation-class findings MUST reach `re_review_passed` before the review phase can be marked completed.
   363	
   364	**Telegram status language:** When reporting review progress, use granular language:
   365	- Instead of: "Agent fixing"
   366	- Use: "Fix applied, proof pending" / "Proof attached, awaiting re-review" / "Re-review passed, merge eligible"
   367	
   368	## 6b. Gate Exceptions (PRJ-303)
   369	
   370	When a gate MUST be bypassed, use a named exception. See `~/.claude/reference/exception-template.md`.
   371	
   372	**Exception types (closed list):** `emergency_hotfix`, `infrastructure_unavailable`, `owner_override`, `time_critical_deployment`, `atomic_replacement`.
   373	
   374	### Atomic Replacement Exception (PRJ-329)
   375	
   376	Use `atomic_replacement` when a large rebuild replaces files wholesale (deletions >= insertions
   377	OR net change <= 100 LOC). The `enforce-loc-ceiling.sh` hook validates:
   378	1. Net LOC: `deletions >= insertions` OR `(insertions - deletions) <= 100`
   379	2. File overlap: Jaccard index of staged files vs recorded `affected_files` >= 0.8
   380	3. Stats accuracy: recorded `insertions`/`deletions` within 20% of actual
   381	
   382	Decision entry must include: `affected_files`, `insertions`, `deletions`, `net_change`, `justification`.
   383	Codex must have reviewed the full diff (not just delta). See `reference/exception-template.md`.
   384	
   385	**To record an exception:**
   386	1. Load `~/.claude/reference/exception-template.md`
   387	2. Fill in: exception type, gate bypassed, reason, risk, compensating action
   388	3. Append to `.dw-state.json` decisions array with `gate: "exception"`
   389	4. Emit `gate_bypass_used` governance event via `log_governance_event`
   390	5. Include exception summary in PR description
   391	
   392	Gate bypass WITHOUT a named exception is logged as a governance event and flagged in weekly monitoring.
   393	
   394	## 7. Completion
   395	
   396	After `dw-finalize` returns:
   397	1. Delete `.dw-state.json`
   398	2. Output summary: issue, branch, PR URL, merge status
   399	
   400	## Anti-Patterns
   401	
   402	| Bad | Good |
   403	|-----|------|
   404	| Reading dev-workflow-steps.md for instructions | Invoke the step skill — it HAS the instructions |
   405	| Skipping a step skill because "it's simple" | Every step gets its skill invoked, every time |
   406	| Improvising the commit sequence | Invoke dw-deliver — it has the exact sequence |
   407	| Writing evidence files "later" | dw-verify writes evidence as its primary output |
   408	| Asking user "should I continue?" after compact | Read .dw-state.json and resume automatically |
   409	| Grouping tasks ("IDENTIFY → BRANCH → DISCOVER" as one task) | One TaskCreate per step. Always. |
   410	| Doing step work inline instead of invoking the skill | Every step MUST use Skill(skill="dw-*"). The skill may have evolved. |
   411	| "This is trivial, skip the review" | The thought itself is the red flag. HPH-1027: Codex found SECURITY HIGH on a "trivial" change. |
   412	| Compressing steps to "move quickly" | Speed comes from doing the steps efficiently, not from skipping them. |
   413	| Editing files in another repo directly | Spawn agent team teammate in the target repo. Cross-project edits break hook gate resolution. |


</details>

<!-- call_id: tool_DMC82Rgbqua5qCz3Z2x0gNhq -->
<system>844 lines read from file starting from line 1. Total lines in file: 844. End of file reached.</system>
     1	---
     2	name: dw-agent-team
     3	version: 2.0.0
     4	description: "Agent team execution model. The only execution model in v7. Teammates implement with Codex gates, lead orchestrates and merges."
     5	type: rigid
     6	---
     7	> **dev-workflow release:** v8.26.0
     8	
     9	# DW Agent Team — Separation of Duties Execution
    10	
    11	<CRITICAL>
    12	This is the ONLY execution model for dev-workflow v7. Solo self-gating is removed.
    13	
    14	Agent teams enforce separation of duties:
    15	- **Teammate** = implementer. Writes code. Runs dw-* skills. Runs straight-through with Codex gates.
    16	- **Lead** = orchestrator. Runs Codex review after teammate completes. Auto-proceeds on verdicts. Merges PRs.
    17	
    18	**Skill updates, documentation changes, and AGENTS.md edits are implementation work — spawn a teammate for them just like production code.** The lead's role does not change: spawn, review, merge.
    19	
    20	Teammates run autonomously with Codex at all gates. Lead validates via Codex after completion.
    21	</CRITICAL>
    22	
    23	<CRITICAL>
    24	**MAX 3 CONCURRENT AGENTS — OAuth Token Race Condition**
    25	
    26	Claude Code v2.1.x has a confirmed OAuth token refresh race condition (#37520, #37324, #24317).
    27	The OAuth refresh token is single-use — when one agent refreshes it, the old token is invalidated
    28	server-side. Other agents still holding the old token get 401 / "Not logged in" errors.
    29	The lock mechanism has only 5 retries / ~7.5s max wait, insufficient for 4+ concurrent processes.
    30	
    31	**Mitigations (remove when Anthropic fixes #37520):**
    32	1. Max 3 teammates in any wave (was 4)
    33	2. Stagger spawns: 30s between each (4x safety margin over 7.5s lock window)
    34	3. See "Token Expiry Recovery" section below if it happens anyway
    35	</CRITICAL>
    36	
    37	## Prerequisites
    38	
    39	Enable agent teams in settings.json:
    40	```json
    41	{
    42	  "env": {
    43	    "CLAUDE_CODE_EXPERIMENTAL_AGENT_TEAMS": "1"
    44	  }
    45	}
    46	```
    47	
    48	Requires Claude Code v2.1.32+.
    49	
    50	## When to Use
    51	
    52	**Single ticket:** Lead spawns 1 teammate. Teammate implements. Lead validates via Codex.
    53	**Multiple tickets:** Lead spawns 2-3 teammates. They claim tasks. Lead validates each via Codex.
    54	
    55	### Parallel Batch Execution (PRJ-758/759/760 pilot)
    56	
    57	When the user drops 2–4 small tickets at once (≤3 files each, Low blast radius, no cross-dependencies), run them in parallel:
    58	
    59	1. **Create all worktrees first** — one per ticket, same date prefix
    60	2. **Initialize `.dw-state.json`** in each with `identify` and `branch` pre-marked `completed`
    61	3. **Spawn teammates** — stagger by 30s (OAuth race #37520)
    62	4. **Each teammate runs straight-through:** discover → implement → verify → review → deliver → PR
    63	5. **Lead reviews each PR independently** via `codex review --base main` from the worktree
    64	6. **Merge in any order** — files don't overlap, so no conflicts
    65	
    66	**When NOT to parallelize:**
    67	- Tickets touch the same files (merge conflicts)
    68	- Any ticket is Medium/High blast radius with schema/auth/CI changes
    69	- Total combined LOC > 500 (ceiling hook blocks)
    70	- Tickets have logical dependencies (B builds on A)
    71	
    72	**Lead step budget for 3 parallel tickets:** ~15 steps total (3 spawns + 3 review cycles + 3 merges) vs ~90–150 steps if done linearly by the lead.
    73	**Always:** This is the only execution model. Used for both Fast and Standard paths.
    74	
    75	### Why Agent Team Even for Single Tickets
    76	
    77	The lead has a 100-step context limit. Implementation (writing code, running tests, fixing Codex findings) burns 30-50 steps per ticket. If the lead writes code directly, the step limit is hit mid-work and the session dies.
    78	
    79	**The teammate has their own step budget.** The lead only spends ~5 steps per ticket:
    80	1. Spawn teammate (~1 step)
    81	2. Wait for completion notification (~0 steps — background)
    82	3. Lead Codex review from worktree (~1 step)
    83	4. State File Handoff + merge (~2-3 steps)
    84	
    85	**Rule: always spawn at least 1 teammate, even for trivial tickets. Never write implementation code as lead.**
    86	
    87	## Architecture
    88	
    89	```
    90	Lead (you / orchestrator Claude)
    91	├── Creates team via TeamCreate
    92	├── Creates shared tasks with dependencies
    93	├── Runs codex review from worktree after teammate completes
    94	├── Auto-proceeds on Codex APPROVE, stops on REJECT
    95	├── Copies .dw-state.json from worktree to main repo (State File Handoff)
    96	├── Removes worktree, then merges PR
    97	├── Runs FINALIZE per ticket
    98	└── Never writes implementation code
    99	
   100	Teammate (full Claude Code instance, general-purpose)
   101	├── Loads CLAUDE.md, skills, hooks, MCP servers automatically
   102	├── Claims tasks from shared task list
   103	├── Runs dw-* skills straight-through (Semgrep + security review, no Codex)
   104	├── Creates PR, writes skip decision (reviewer_role: "teammate", gate: "skipped")
   105	└── Does NOT merge — lead runs sole Codex review and merges
   106	```
   107	
   108	**Agent type matters:** Teammates MUST be spawned as `general-purpose` (the default).
   109	NEVER use `Explore` — it's read-only and cannot `SendMessage` back to the lead.
   110	NEVER use `Plan` — it can't edit files. Only `general-purpose` has full tool access
   111	including SendMessage for gate communication.
   112	
   113	## Lead Protocol
   114	
   115	### 1. Setup
   116	
   117	Create worktree base directory and per-ticket worktrees:
   118	```bash
   119	WORKTREE_BASE="/tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/$(date +%Y%m%d)"
   120	mkdir -p "$WORKTREE_BASE"
   121	
   122	# For each ticket, create the worktree (no spawn marker yet — written just before each Agent call)
   123	WORKTREE="$WORKTREE_BASE/TICKET-ID"
   124	git worktree add "$WORKTREE" -b feature/TICKET-ID main  # new branch
   125	# OR: git worktree add "$WORKTREE" existing-branch-name  # existing branch
   126	
   127	# PRJ-744: Remove stale evidence files that git may restore into the worktree
   128	# because they were historically tracked. Keeps evidence from leaking across tickets.
   129	# Only remove untracked files; if still tracked, untrack with git rm --cached.
   130	for _ev in .code-review-evidence.md .verification-evidence.md .discovery-notes.md .implementation-plan.md; do
   131	    if [[ -f "$WORKTREE/$_ev" ]]; then
   132	        if git -C "$WORKTREE" ls-files --error-unmatch "$_ev" >/dev/null 2>&1; then
   133	            git -C "$WORKTREE" rm --cached "$_ev" >/dev/null 2>&1 || true
   134	        else
   135	            rm -f "$WORKTREE/$_ev"
   136	        fi
   137	    fi
   138	done
   139	```
   140	
   141	### 2. Create Team
   142	
   143	Spawn teammates. 2-3 for multi-ticket work, 1 for single ticket.
   144	
   145	**CRITICAL: Write `.agent-spawned` immediately before EACH Agent tool call** (not during batch setup).
   146	The marker tells the watchdog "an agent is about to start." Writing it too early (e.g., during
   147	upfront worktree creation) causes false "never started" alerts for queued tickets waiting more
   148	than 5 minutes before their spawn. The sequence for each teammate:
   149	```bash
   150	# Step A: write marker (must land on disk before Agent call)
   151	# Format: timestamp|lead_session_id — watchdog uses the session ID to distinguish
   152	# the lead's own heartbeat (not proof of teammate start) from the teammate's.
   153	printf '%s|%s\n' "$(date +%s)" "${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID:-}" > "$WORKTREE/.agent-spawned"
   154	# Step B: immediately invoke Agent tool (within same shell turn)
   155	```
   156	Ordering guarantee: the marker is always on disk before the agent runs, so the watchdog's strict
   157	`HEARTBEAT_MTIME >= SPAWN_TIME` comparison is valid — any legitimate heartbeat from this spawn
   158	has mtime >= spawn_time, and a fast-starting agent can never emit a heartbeat before the marker.
   159	
   160	**MANDATORY: Stagger spawns by 30 seconds** to avoid OAuth token refresh race condition:
   161	```
   162	Spawn agent 1 → wait 30s → spawn agent 2 → wait 30s → spawn agent 3
   163	```
   164	Each agent must complete its initial OAuth handshake before the next one starts.
   165	The token refresh lock window is ~7.5s, so 30s gives a 4x safety margin.
   166	
   167	```
   168	Create an agent team. Spawn [N] teammates to implement tickets.
   169	Each teammate follows the full dev-workflow path and messages me
   170	at every gate with proof before proceeding.
   171	Use Opus for teammates (model: "opus" — 1M context prevents context exhaustion on Standard path).
   172	IMPORTANT: Wait 30 seconds between each spawn (OAuth race condition mitigation).
   173	```
   174	
   175	Or use the TeamCreate tool directly if available. Still stagger by 30s between each.
   176	
   177	### 2.5. First-Session Progress Monitor (Optional but Recommended)
   178	
   179	On your **first agent-team session** (or when running new teammate configurations),
   180	start the log-growth watcher in the background immediately after spawning teammates:
   181	
   182	```bash
   183	# Find the Kimi session tasks directory (varies by session)
   184	TASK_DIR="$(find "$HOME/.kimi/sessions" -name 'agent-*' -type d -path '*/tasks/*' 2>/dev/null | head -1 | xargs dirname 2>/dev/null)"
   185	if [[ -n "$TASK_DIR" ]]; then
   186	    nohup bash "$MAIN_REPO/scripts/agent-team-watch.sh" "$TASK_DIR" 300 >/tmp/agent-team-watch.log 2>&1 &
   187	    echo "Progress watcher PID: $!"
   188	fi
   189	```
   190	
   191	This watcher:
   192	- Checks each teammate's output log size every 5 minutes (configurable)
   193	- Alerts via Telegram if a teammate's log hasn't grown (possible freeze/OAuth issue)
   194	- Exits automatically when all teammates complete
   195	
   196	**When to skip:** If `agent-watchdog.sh` is already running and you are confident
   197	in the teammate spawn pipeline, the watchdog handles the same concern via heartbeat
   198	files. Use the log watcher as a belt-and-suspenders measure for first sessions.
   199	
   200	### 3. Create Tasks with Dependencies
   201	
   202	Create tasks in the shared task list. Map waves to dependencies:
   203	
   204	```
   205	Tasks for the team:
   206	
   207	Wave 1 (no dependencies):
   208	- "VMP-2670: Fix employee sync — full dev-workflow, worktree at [path]"
   209	- "VMP-2675: Extract graph-utils — full dev-workflow, worktree at [path]"
   210	
   211	Wave 2 (depends on Wave 1):
   212	- "VMP-2671: Ingest shifts" (depends on VMP-2670)
   213	- "VMP-2676: View modes" (depends on VMP-2675)
   214	
   215	Wave 3 (depends on Wave 2):
   216	- "VMP-2672: works_with connections" (depends on VMP-2671)
   217	```
   218	
   219	When Wave 1 tasks complete, Wave 2 tasks auto-unblock. Teammates self-claim.
   220	
   221	### 4. Post-Completion Validation (v7 — Codex Auto-Proceed)
   222	
   223	Teammates run straight-through. Lead validates AFTER teammate completes, not during.
   224	
   225	**After teammate finishes (PR created + agent-side Codex review done):**
   226	
   227	Lead runs independent Codex review from the **worktree** (defense-in-depth). The Codex invocation uses `scripts/codex-review-wrapper.sh` (PRJ-655) — the single source of truth for `codex review --base` invocations. The wrapper injects the severity policy (PRJ-640) into AGENTS.md, appends the output-format block, optionally appends `.implementation-plan.md`, hides the mutation from git via `--assume-unchanged`, and restores AGENTS.md on EXIT/INT/TERM. It also skips injection entirely if the feature branch modifies AGENTS.md (diff-contamination guard). **§6 endgame and the teammate template back-reference this wrapper — do not inline the procedure.**
   228	
   229	```bash
   230	cd /tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/<YYYYMMDD>/<ticket-id>
   231	
   232	# Canonical injected-review procedure (PRJ-640, extracted to wrapper in PRJ-655).
   233	# Single source of truth: scripts/codex-review-wrapper.sh. The wrapper handles
   234	# severity policy injection, output-format block, optional plan context, AGENTS.md
   235	# backup/restore, assume-unchanged bit, and EXIT/INT/TERM trap. It also skips
   236	# injection when the feature branch modifies AGENTS.md (diff-contamination guard).
   237	bash "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/scripts/codex-review-wrapper.sh" \
   238	  --base main --inject-plan
   239	```
   240	
   241	**IMPORTANT:** Run from the worktree where the feature branch is checked out. Running from the main repo produces an empty diff (you're on main). The `--pr` flag does not exist on `codex review`.
   242	
   243	| Lead Codex Verdict | Action |
   244	|-------------------|--------|
   245	| APPROVE + CI green | Proceed to State File Handoff → Merge |
   246	| REQUEST_CHANGES | Notify via Telegram with specific findings. Stop. |
   247	| REJECT | Notify via Telegram. Stop. |
   248	| PR checks failing | Wait for CI. If still failing, notify via Telegram. Stop. |
   249	
   250	**On REQUEST_CHANGES:** The lead does NOT wait for human input. The findings are logged, the PR is left open, and the issue is flagged in Telegram. The user can resume the fix cycle in a future session.
   251	
   252	Max 3 automatic fix cycles (lead instructs teammate to fix → teammate pushes → lead re-reviews). If still rejected → stop and notify via Telegram.
   253	
   254	**Lead owner_override (if all findings are WAIVABLE):**
   255	If Codex returns REQUEST_CHANGES but all findings are out-of-scope (follow-on work, adjacent concerns) and you are the lead:
   256	
   257	```bash
   258	# In the worktree
   259	source ~/.claude/hooks/gate-helpers.sh
   260	HEAD_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD)
   261	PR_NUM=$(jq -r '.durable_ids.pr_number' .dw-state.json)
   262	EXCEPTION_JSON=$(_record_gate_exception "pr-review" "owner_override" \
   263	  "Justification for override (e.g., 'All findings out-of-scope, ticketed PRJ-XXX')" "low" \
   264	  "Linear issues created: [ID list]" "codex" "lead" \
   265	  "$PR_NUM" "$HEAD_SHA" \
   266	  "" \
   267	  "false" \
   268	  2>/dev/null | grep '^\s*{' | head -1)
   269	# 10th arg is classification (PRJ-753, may be empty for legacy paths); 11th arg is false_block (PRJ-846): pass "true" if you bypassed because the parser/matcher was wrong, "false" otherwise (default).
   270	_dw_append_decision "$EXCEPTION_JSON"
   271	```
   272	
   273	Then proceed to State File Handoff → Merge (steps 5-9 below).
   274	
   275	### 5. State File Handoff (MANDATORY before merge)
   276	
   277	The teammate's `.dw-state.json` lives in the worktree. The `require-pr-review.sh`
   278	hook checks the **main repo** directory. Without this handoff, `gh pr merge` is BLOCKED.
   279	
   280	**Note (PRJ-643):** The aggregate `codex_rounds_total` counter (and paired
   281	`codex_rounds_cap`) rides along with the state file during handoff — no
   282	separate copy step. The lead's Codex round runs from the worktree, which
   283	increments the worktree counter; the subsequent whole-file copy carries the
   284	updated value into the main repo. No code change needed in this section.
   285	
   286	**IMPORTANT:** The handoff process differs based on whether the lead approved or recorded an exception:
   287	
   288	**5a. HANDOFF PATH: Codex APPROVE**
   289	
   290	After the lead runs Codex review and approves:
   291	```bash
   292	# Copy teammate's state and evidence artifacts from worktree to main repo
   293	WORKTREE="/tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/<YYYYMMDD>/<ticket-id>"
   294	MAIN_REPO="<path-to-main-repo>"
   295	
   296	cp "$WORKTREE/.dw-state.json" "$MAIN_REPO/.dw-state.json"
   297	[[ -f "$WORKTREE/.task-progress.json" ]] && cp "$WORKTREE/.task-progress.json" "$MAIN_REPO/.task-progress.json"
   298	
   299	# Clear execution_context (handoff complete; lead is the implicit context in main repo).
   300	# Copied state file still says "teammate", which would block the lead's gh pr merge via
   301	# _is_teammate_context() OR logic. PRJ-580: clear instead of flipping to "lead" — the
   302	# helper's missing-field default ("lead") is equivalent to explicit "lead" for the merge
   303	# gate, and clearing avoids the post-handoff catch-22 when stale state is resumed.
   304	source ~/.claude/hooks/gate-helpers.sh
   305	_dw_clear_execution_context "$MAIN_REPO/.dw-state.json"
   306	
   307	# Also copy evidence files (namespace by ticket ID for batch runs)
   308	TICKET_ID=$(jq -r '.issue' "$WORKTREE/.dw-state.json")
   309	[[ -f "$WORKTREE/.code-review-evidence.md" ]] && cp "$WORKTREE/.code-review-evidence.md" "$MAIN_REPO/.code-review-evidence-${TICKET_ID}.md"
   310	[[ -f "$WORKTREE/.verification-evidence.md" ]] && cp "$WORKTREE/.verification-evidence.md" "$MAIN_REPO/.verification-evidence-${TICKET_ID}.md"
   311	```
   312	> **If step 4 shows BEHIND:** After rebase and re-review with the new HEAD, repeat steps 5–6 (re-copy state file and evidence files with new HEAD before merging).
   313	
   314	```bash
   315	# PRJ-329: Update pr-review to completed with lead's APPROVE verdict INCLUDING reviewer_role + head_sha
   316	cd "$MAIN_REPO"
   317	source ~/.claude/hooks/gate-helpers.sh
   318	HEAD_SHA=$(git -C "$WORKTREE" rev-parse HEAD 2>/dev/null || echo "unknown")
   319	PR_NUM=$(gh pr list --head "$(jq -r '.branch' .dw-state.json)" --json number --jq '.[0].number' 2>/dev/null || echo "null")
   320	TS=$(date -u +%FT%TZ)
   321	DECISION=$(jq -nc --arg sha "$HEAD_SHA" --arg pr "$PR_NUM" --arg repo "$MAIN_REPO" --arg ts "$TS" \
   322	  '{step:"pr-review",gate:"codex",command:"codex review --base main",verdict:"APPROVE",reviewer_role:"lead",pr_number:($pr|tonumber),head_sha:$sha,repo_context:$repo,timestamp:$ts}') \
   323	  && _dw_append_decision "$DECISION" \
   324	  && _dw_set_phase_completed "pr-review"
   325	```
   326	
   327	**Why the `&&` chain (fail-fast, not transactional):** The original
   328	single-jq filter was a single rename — all-or-nothing. The helper-based
   329	sequence is two separate atomic renames chained with `&&`. This is
   330	**fail-fast, not all-or-nothing**: if DECISION construction or the
   331	decision append fails (e.g. PR_NUM is "null" and `($pr|tonumber)` errors),
   332	the phase is NOT marked completed. **However:** if `_dw_set_phase_completed`
   333	itself fails after the decision was already persisted, the state is
   334	partially updated — the APPROVE decision is in `.dw-state.json` but the
   335	phase is not yet marked completed. Recovery: re-running this block
   336	re-appends the same decision (duplicate, harmless — the merge gate
   337	matches on most-recent verdict for this PR) and retries the phase mark.
   338	This trade-off is documented in `docs/b1-state-write-helpers-inventory.md`
   339	("two separate calls — cleaner, slightly less atomic but each step is
   340	already idempotent"). True transactional semantics across the two writes
   341	would require a B6-class change.
   342	
   343	**5b. HANDOFF PATH: owner_override exception (REQUEST_CHANGES + WAIVABLE findings)**
   344	
   345	If the lead recorded an owner_override exception, the exception is already in `.dw-state.json` on the worktree (from step 4 above).
   346	Copy state and evidence files, then mark `pr-review` as completed WITHOUT appending any `APPROVE` decision:
   347	
   348	```bash
   349	# Copy teammate's state and evidence artifacts from worktree to main repo
   350	WORKTREE="/tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/<YYYYMMDD>/<ticket-id>"
   351	MAIN_REPO="<path-to-main-repo>"
   352	
   353	cp "$WORKTREE/.dw-state.json" "$MAIN_REPO/.dw-state.json"
   354	[[ -f "$WORKTREE/.task-progress.json" ]] && cp "$WORKTREE/.task-progress.json" "$MAIN_REPO/.task-progress.json"
   355	
   356	# Clear execution_context (same reason as 5a path; PRJ-580: clear, don't flip to "lead")
   357	source ~/.claude/hooks/gate-helpers.sh
   358	_dw_clear_execution_context "$MAIN_REPO/.dw-state.json"
   359	
   360	# Also copy evidence files
   361	TICKET_ID=$(jq -r '.issue' "$WORKTREE/.dw-state.json")
   362	[[ -f "$WORKTREE/.code-review-evidence.md" ]] && cp "$WORKTREE/.code-review-evidence.md" "$MAIN_REPO/.code-review-evidence-${TICKET_ID}.md"
   363	[[ -f "$WORKTREE/.verification-evidence.md" ]] && cp "$WORKTREE/.verification-evidence.md" "$MAIN_REPO/.verification-evidence-${TICKET_ID}.md"
   364	```
   365	
   366	```bash
   367	# PRJ-465: Update pr-review to completed WITHOUT appending APPROVE — exception is already in decisions array
   368	cd "$MAIN_REPO"
   369	source ~/.claude/hooks/gate-helpers.sh
   370	_dw_set_phase_completed "pr-review"
   371	```
   372	
   373	**Do NOT append any verdict decision.** The exception in the decisions array is the only pr-review artifact.
   374	The merge gate (`require-pr-review.sh`) accepts EITHER an explicit APPROVE decision OR a valid owner_override exception.
   375	
   376	**Why this exists:** In the March 24 2026 session, the lead ran Codex review successfully but
   377	`gh pr merge` was BLOCKED because `.dw-state.json` only existed in the worktree. The lead had
   378	to manually construct a state file — fragile and error-prone. This handoff protocol prevents that.
   379	
   380	### 6. Formalized Endgame Sequence (PRJ-329)
   381	
   382	<CRITICAL>
   383	Follow this exact numbered sequence. Do NOT skip steps or reorder.
   384	
   385	1. Teammate work complete (all 3 gates passed)
   386	2. Lead runs independent `codex review --base main` from **worktree** via the wrapper documented in §4 (`scripts/codex-review-wrapper.sh --base main --inject-plan`, PRJ-655). Do not run a bare `codex review --base main` here — it skips severity policy injection.
   387	3. Lead validates verdict is explicit (not blank/empty)
   388	4. Lead writes decision to worktree `.dw-state.json` with `reviewer_role: "lead"`, `head_sha`, `pr_number`
   389	5. State File Handoff: copy `.dw-state.json` from worktree to main repo (see above)
   390	6. Mark `pr-review` phase as `completed` in main repo `.dw-state.json` via `_dw_set_phase_completed "pr-review"` (chained after the decision-write helper call in §5a/5b)
   391	7. **cd to main repo** before merging. Verify: `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` matches main repo path.
   392	8. Remove worktree (frees the branch for --delete-branch):
   393	   ```bash
   394	   git worktree remove /tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/<YYYYMMDD>/<ticket-id>
   395	   ```
   396	9. Merge: `gh pr merge <PR#> --squash --delete-branch`
   397	10. Post-merge verification: `gh pr view <PR#> --json state` confirms `MERGED`
   398	11. Linear update + Telegram notification
   399	12. State cleanup (handled automatically by `cleanup-state-post-merge.sh` hook)
   400	</CRITICAL>
   401	
   402	**Wrong-CWD protection (PRJ-329):** ALWAYS cd to the main repo before running `gh pr merge`.
   403	Verify with `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` that you are in the correct repo. The repo path
   404	must match `.dw-state.json` location. Running merge from the worktree produces confusing errors.
   405	
   406	For multi-ticket merges, process in dependency order. After each merge:
   407	1. Rebase dependent branches in remaining worktrees: `git -C <worktree> fetch origin main && git -C <worktree> merge origin/main`
   408	2. Run FINALIZE for the merged ticket (Linear update)
   409	3. Notify team: "VMP-XXXX merged. Dependent tasks unblocked."
   410	
   411	### 7. Cleanup
   412	
   413	After all tickets complete:
   414	```
   415	Clean up the team
   416	```
   417	Then remove any remaining worktrees:
   418	```bash
   419	git worktree list | grep "$WORKTREE_BASE" | awk '{print $1}' | xargs -I{} git worktree remove {}
   420	# Clean up any leftover state files
   421	rm -f <main-repo>/.dw-state.json
   422	rm -f <main-repo>/.task-progress.json
   423	```
   424	
   425	## Large Diff Mitigation: Two-Spawn Pattern
   426	
   427	When a ticket involves large hook or skill changes, a single teammate's
   428	IMPLEMENT phase can exceed the 900s timeout — even with no Codex review in
   429	scope (PRJ-745). PRJ-747 demonstrated this: ~280 LOC across 7 hook files
   430	caused the teammate to time out twice during IMPLEMENT alone, forcing the
   431	lead to burn ~30-40 steps on direct implementation.
   432	
   433	**Threshold:** Use the two-spawn pattern when the discover scope shows:
   434	- Hook or skill changes ≥ 200 LOC, OR
   435	- Hook or skill changes touching ≥ 4 files
   436	
   437	These thresholds are heuristic — derived from PRJ-747 empirical data.
   438	
   439	### Pattern
   440	
   441	**Spawn 1 (long — DISCOVER → PLAN → IMPLEMENT):**
   442	- Runs: IDENTIFY → BRANCH → DISCOVER → PLAN → IMPLEMENT
   443	- Stops after `dw-implement` completes. Does NOT commit.
   444	- Leaves uncommitted changes and `.dw-state.json` in the worktree.
   445	- State file must show: `current_phase: "implement"`, `phases.implement.status: "completed"`
   446	- Writes `.agent-spawned` at start. Writes `.agent-done` at completion so the
   447	  watchdog knows the agent finished its phase.
   448	
   449	**Spawn 2 (short — VERIFY → DELIVER → PR):**
   450	- Reads `.dw-state.json` to confirm spawn 1 completed implement.
   451	- Runs: SCOPE-CHECK → VERIFY → SIMPLIFY → REVIEW → DELIVER → PR
   452	- Commits the changes spawn 1 wrote, then proceeds through verification,
   453	  review, and delivery.
   454	- Writes `.agent-spawned` at start, `.agent-done` at completion.
   455	
   456	### Lead Protocol for Two-Spawn
   457	
   458	**Pre-spawn assessment (preferred):** Before spawning, the lead reads the
   459	ticket description and does a quick scope check. If the ticket is clearly a
   460	large hook/skill change (based on description, known history, or a quick
   461	`git diff --stat` against main for similar past tickets), use two-spawn from
   462	the start. Tell spawn 1: "Use the two-spawn pattern. Stop after IMPLEMENT.
   463	Do not commit."
   464	
   465	**Teammate-discovered assessment (fallback):** If the lead is uncertain,
   466	spawn with the spawn-1 prompt from the Two-Spawn Variant Prompts section
   467	below. The teammate assesses scope during `dw-discover`. If it hits the
   468	threshold, it continues through IMPLEMENT and then stops. If it does NOT hit
   469	the threshold, it may continue through the full standard path. The lead then
   470	spawns spawn 2 only if needed.
   471	
   472	**Sequence:**
   473	1. Lead decides (pre-spawn or post-discover) → tells spawn 1 to use two-spawn.
   474	2. Spawn 1 runs and stops after IMPLEMENT.
   475	3. Wait for spawn 1 completion notification.
   476	4. Lead clears `.agent-running` and refreshes `.agent-spawned`.
   477	5. Spawn spawn 2 (30s stagger from any other active spawns).
   478	6. Spawn 2 runs SCOPE-CHECK → VERIFY → SIMPLIFY → REVIEW → DELIVER → PR.
   479	7. Lead proceeds with normal post-completion validation and merge.
   480	
   481	### Spawn 2 Setup (Resume, Not Bootstrap)
   482	
   483	Unlike a normal teammate spawn, spawn 2 **must not** overwrite `.dw-state.json`.
   484	It reuses the state file left by spawn 1:
   485	
   486	```bash
   487	# Verify spawn 1 completed implement
   488	if [[ "$(jq -r '.phases.implement.status' .dw-state.json 2>/dev/null)" != "completed" ]]; then
   489	    echo "ERROR: Spawn 1 did not complete implement phase. Stopping."
   490	    exit 1
   491	fi
   492	
   493	# Resume from the next phase instead of bootstrapping fresh
   494	_TF=$(mktemp)
   495	jq '.current_phase = "scope-check" | .phases["scope-check"] = {"status": "pending"}' \
   496	  .dw-state.json > "$_TF" && mv -f "$_TF" .dw-state.json
   497	```
   498	
   499	### Handoff Contract
   500	
   501	Spawn 1 → spawn 2 handoff is via the worktree filesystem:
   502	- Uncommitted code changes in the worktree
   503	- `.dw-state.json` with implement phase completed
   504	- `.task-progress.json` updated if task progress is enabled
   505	
   506	**Lead cleanup before spawn 2:**
   507	```bash
   508	# Clear watchdog ownership so spawn 2 can enroll on its first heartbeat
   509	rm -f "$WORKTREE/.agent-running"
   510	# Refresh spawn marker so watchdog tracks spawn 2, not spawn 1
   511	printf '%s|%s\n' "$(date +%s)" "${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID:-}" > "$WORKTREE/.agent-spawned"
   512	```
   513	
   514	### Why This Works
   515	
   516	- Spawn 1's scope is narrower: no VERIFY tests, no REVIEW, no DELIVER
   517	  commit/push, no PR creation.
   518	- Spawn 2's scope is lighter: no file-writing discovery, no plan creation,
   519	  no implementation reasoning.
   520	- Each spawn is well under 900s. PRJ-747's IMPLEMENT was the sole timeout
   521	  driver; verification and delivery are comparatively fast.
   522	
   523	## Teammate Spawn Prompt Template (v7 — Straight-Through)
   524	
   525	Each teammate gets this as their spawn prompt. Teammates run straight-through
   526	with Codex at all gates — no human pauses. Lead validates after completion.
   527	
   528	**For large diffs (≥200 LOC or ≥4 files):** Use the Two-Spawn Pattern
   529	documented above. Spawn 1 stops after the IMPLEMENT step in Phase 2.
   530	Spawn 2 runs from SCOPE-CHECK through Phase 3.
   531	
   532	```
   533	You are an autonomous implementer on an agent team. Run the full dev-workflow
   534	Standard path straight through — Codex replaces human at all gates.
   535	Do NOT stop or wait for approval. Complete all steps and create the PR.
   536	
   537	**Scope includes ALL implementation work:** code changes, skill file updates, documentation edits, and AGENTS.md modifications. If the ticket touches any of these, implement them fully — do not defer to the lead.
   538	
   539	Ticket: [TICKET-ID] — [title] | Worktree: [path]
   540	
   541	## For Each Task You Claim
   542	
   543	### Setup
   544	1. Read the task description for the ticket ID and worktree path
   545	2. cd to the pre-created worktree. The lead creates worktrees before spawning (since v8.7.0).
   546	   If the worktree does not exist for any reason, create it using the dated path:
   547	   git worktree add /tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/$(date +%Y%m%d)/TICKET-ID -b feature/TICKET-ID main
   548	   **CRITICAL:** The lead writes `.agent-spawned` to the worktree in Setup (step 1), BEFORE issuing the spawn request. By the time you start, the marker is already on disk. If you don't see `.agent-spawned` by the time you reach step 3, the watchdog cannot detect if you freeze before your first tool call — contact the lead immediately.
   549	3. Create .dw-state.json in the worktree — REQUIRED FIELDS including execution_context:
   550	   ```bash
   551	   cat > .dw-state.json <<'STATEOF'
   552	   {
   553	     "version": "8.0",
   554	     "task_progress_enabled": true,
   555	     "task_progress_enforcement": "hook",
   556	     "codex_level_skip_enabled": true,
   557	     "path": "standard",
   558	     "execution_model": "agent_team",
   559	     "execution_context": "teammate",
   560	     "current_phase": "identify",
   561	     "issue": "TICKET-ID",
   562	     "branch": "feature/TICKET-ID",
   563	     "phases": {},
   564	     "decisions": [],
   565	     "durable_ids": {}
   566	   }
   567	   STATEOF
   568	   ```
   569	   `codex_level_skip_enabled: true` opts this workflow into the docs-only
   570	   `codex_level=lite` skip pilot (PRJ-652). `dw-review` and `dw-pr-review` check
   571	   this flag before writing skip decisions. Without it, skip paths are inert and
   572	   reviews run as before. Note the matching merge-gate guardrail in
   573	   `require-pr-review.sh` also requires this flag — the skip path cannot be
   574	   activated by hand-editing state alone.
   575	
   576	   The `"execution_context": "teammate"` field is **mandatory**. It is the runtime role signal
   577	   that allows `require-pr-review.sh` to block your merge attempts mechanically. Without it,
   578	   the hook falls back to path-based detection only. Both signals are needed for defense-in-depth.
   579	
   580	### Phase 1: Plan (IDENTIFY → PLAN)
   581	Run these skills IN ORDER in the worktree:
   582	- Skill(skill="dw-identify")
   583	- Skill(skill="dw-branch") — branch already exists from worktree, just verify
   584	- Skill(skill="dw-discover")
   585	- Skill(skill="dw-plan") — writes .implementation-plan.md, then proceeds directly to IMPLEMENT
   586	- Codex reviews the committed diff at Phase 2 (REVIEW) and Phase 3 (PR-REVIEW). No plan-time Codex gate. (PRJ-639, v8.15.0 — dropped dw-validate.)
   587	
   588	### Phase 2: Implement + Review (IMPLEMENT → REVIEW)
   589	- Skill(skill="dw-implement") — write code per plan
   590	- Skill(skill="dw-scope-check") — verify files match plan, ≤500 LOC
   591	- Skill(skill="dw-verify") — typecheck, build, test
   592	- Skill(skill="dw-simplify") — conditional simplification
   593	- Skill(skill="dw-review") — Semgrep + security review (haiku if available). **Teammate does NOT run Codex.**
   594	- Fix any security findings. If Semgrep or security review rejects after 1 fix → exit with blocked status.
   595	
   596	### Phase 3: Deliver + PR (DELIVER → PR creation + lead-only review)
   597	- Skill(skill="dw-deliver") — commit + push
   598	- Create PR with gh pr create
   599	- Lead runs `codex review --base main` after teammate completes. Teammate does NOT run Codex.
   600	- **Persist PR number immediately after `gh pr create`:**
   601	  ```bash
   602	  STATE_FILE="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.dw-state.json"
   603	  PR_NUM=$(gh pr list --head "$(git rev-parse --abbrev-ref HEAD)" --json number --jq '.[0].number')
   604	  _TFS=$(mktemp "$(dirname "$STATE_FILE")/.dw-state.XXXXXX")
   605	  jq --arg pr "$PR_NUM" '.durable_ids.pr_number = ($pr | tonumber)' "$STATE_FILE" > "$_TFS" && mv -f "$_TFS" "$STATE_FILE"
   606	  ```
   607	- Write skip decision entry with reviewer_role: "teammate" (the teammate never runs Codex; the lead is the sole Codex gate). The `.dw-state.json` entry is still written by the orchestrator via jq (single-writer contract). The `.task-progress.json` entry is written EXCLUSIVELY by the PostToolUse `track-task-update.sh` hook when you call TaskUpdate with metadata:
   608	  ```bash
   609	  STATE_FILE="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.dw-state.json"
   610	  HEAD_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD 2>/dev/null)
   611	  _TS=$(date -u +%FT%TZ)
   612	  DECISION=$(jq -nc --arg sha "$HEAD_SHA" --arg ts "$_TS" \
   613	    '{step:"pr-review",reviewer_role:"teammate",gate:"skipped",head_sha:$sha,timestamp:$ts,reason:"lead-only merge gate — teammate does not run Codex"}')
   614	  _TFS=$(mktemp "$(dirname "$STATE_FILE")/.dw-state.XXXXXX")
   615	  jq --argjson d "$DECISION" --arg ts "$_TS" '
   616	    .decisions += [$d] |
   617	    .phases["pr-review"] = {"status": "skipped", "completed_at": $ts} |
   618	    .current_phase = "pr-review" |
   619	    .last_updated = $ts
   620	  ' "$STATE_FILE" > "$_TFS" && mv -f "$_TFS" "$STATE_FILE" || { rm -f "$_TFS"; exit 1; }
   621	  ```
   622	  Then mark the pr-review task skipped via TaskUpdate (PRJ-480 — hook writes `.task-progress.json`):
   623	  ```
   624	  TaskUpdate(taskId: "<pr-review-task-id>", status: "completed",
   625	             metadata: { dw_step: "pr-review",
   626	                         dw_progress_status: "skipped",
   627	                         dw_skip_reason: "lead-only merge gate" })
   628	  ```
   629	  Do NOT jq-write `.task-progress.json` directly — the merge gate rejects actor-authored progress when `task_progress_enforcement="hook"`.
   630	  ```bash
   631	  touch "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.agent-done" 2>/dev/null || true
   632	  ```
   633	- **Validate state file integrity (PRJ-544):**
   634	  ```bash
   635	  _WT_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
   636	  bash ~/.claude/scripts/validate-state-file.sh "$_WT_ROOT/.dw-state.json"
   637	  ```
   638	  If the validator exits non-zero: touch `$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.agent-done`,
   639	  then stop immediately. Report the exact error message to the task list so the lead can diagnose.
   640	
   641	Output at completion: PR URL, PR number, verdict: "skipped" (lead-only gate), LOC stats.
   642	Do NOT merge. `gh pr merge` is FORBIDDEN from teammate context — the hook will block it.
   643	Do NOT invoke dw-pr-review. Lead merges after validation.
   644	
   645	### Two-Spawn Variant Prompts
   646	
   647	When the lead instructs you to use the two-spawn pattern, follow the
   648	appropriate prompt below instead of the standard template.
   649	
   650	**Spawn 1 (long) prompt:**
   651	```
   652	You are autonomous implementer spawn 1 on an agent team. Run dev-workflow
   653	Standard path through IMPLEMENT only. STOP after dw-implement completes.
   654	Do NOT commit. Do NOT run VERIFY, SIMPLIFY, REVIEW, or DELIVER.
   655	
   656	Ticket: [TICKET-ID] | Worktree: [path]
   657	
   658	Setup: same as standard template (create .dw-state.json with execution_context: teammate).
   659	Run: IDENTIFY → BRANCH → DISCOVER → PLAN → IMPLEMENT.
   660	After IMPLEMENT: update .dw-state.json to show implement completed, then STOP.
   661	Write .agent-done to signal completion. Report PR scope and LOC to the lead.
   662	```
   663	
   664	**Spawn 2 (short) prompt:**
   665	```
   666	You are autonomous implementer spawn 2 on an agent team. Resume where spawn 1
   667	left off. Do NOT recreate .dw-state.json — reuse the existing one.
   668	
   669	Ticket: [TICKET-ID] | Worktree: [path]
   670	
   671	Setup:
   672	1. cd to the worktree.
   673	2. Verify .dw-state.json shows phases.implement.status = "completed".
   674	   If not, stop and report to the lead.
   675	3. Update .dw-state.json: set current_phase = "scope-check".
   676	4. The lead has already written `.agent-spawned` before spawning you.
   677	
   678	Run: SCOPE-CHECK → VERIFY → SIMPLIFY → REVIEW → DELIVER → PR.
   679	Follow the standard template's Phase 2 (from SCOPE-CHECK) and Phase 3 exactly.
   680	Write .agent-done at completion.
   681	```
   682	
   683	## Rules
   684	- **NEVER merge PRs.** Only the lead merges. If you attempt `gh pr merge` for any reason,
   685	  `require-pr-review.sh` will block it with "BLOCKED: Merge attempted from teammate context" —
   686	  this is intentional enforcement, not a bug. If you hit this block, stop and report your
   687	  PR URL to the task list. Do NOT attempt to work around the block.
   688	- Create TaskCreate items for each step within your task.
   689	- **Do NOT jq-write `.task-progress.json` (PRJ-480).** The PostToolUse hook `track-task-update.sh` is the sole writer. It bootstraps the file from `.dw-state.json` on the first TaskUpdate carrying `metadata.dw_step`.
   690	- After each Skill(skill="dw-*") completes, mark the task complete via TaskUpdate with metadata: `TaskUpdate(taskId: "<id>", status: "completed", metadata: { dw_step: "<step>", dw_progress_status: "completed" })`. The hook atomically updates `.task-progress.json` and attaches a valid HMAC `hook_signature`.
   691	- For simplify skipped: `TaskUpdate(..., metadata: { dw_step: "simplify", dw_progress_status: "skipped", dw_skip_reason: "<why>" })`. Merge gate accepts `skipped` for `simplify` (any reason), plus `review`/`pr-review` under codex_level=lite.
   692	- If Codex rejects plan or review after 1 revision → exit with blocked status.
   693	- If you hit context pressure (>70%), write .handoff.md and exit.
   694	```
   695	
   696	## Gate Enforcement Hooks
   697	
   698	### PreToolUse: Agent (LIVE — require-agent-team-protocol.sh)
   699	
   700	Blocks `Agent` tool spawns during active dev-workflow sessions when the prompt
   701	contains implementation keywords but lacks the teammate template markers.
   702	Accepts two protocol shapes (v7): gated (Skill() + gate stops) or straight-through
   703	(3+ distinct Skill() + no-merge + reviewer_role). Also blocks `bypassPermissions`
   704	mode unconditionally for implementation agents.
   705	
   706	**Hook-enforced since 2026-03-26.** Cannot be rationalized away.
   707	
   708	### Future Hooks
   709	
   710	These hooks provide additional mechanical enforcement on top of the messaging protocol:
   711	
   712	### TaskCompleted Hook
   713	```bash
   714	#!/bin/bash
   715	# dw-task-completed.sh — Blocks task completion without evidence
   716	# Hook type: TaskCompleted (exit 2 to reject)
   717	
   718	WORKTREE=$(pwd)
   719	TODAY=$(date +%Y-%m-%d)
   720	
   721	# Check for verification evidence
   722	if ! grep -q "$TODAY" "$WORKTREE/.verification-evidence.md" 2>/dev/null; then
   723	  echo "BLOCKED: Missing .verification-evidence.md with today's date" >&2
   724	  exit 2
   725	fi
   726	
   727	# Check for code review evidence
   728	if ! grep -q "$TODAY" "$WORKTREE/.code-review-evidence.md" 2>/dev/null; then
   729	  echo "BLOCKED: Missing .code-review-evidence.md with today's date" >&2
   730	  exit 2
   731	fi
   732	
   733	exit 0
   734	```
   735	
   736	### TeammateIdle Hook
   737	```bash
   738	#!/bin/bash
   739	# dw-teammate-idle.sh — Prevents idle without gate submission
   740	# Hook type: TeammateIdle (exit 2 to send feedback)
   741	
   742	# Check if there's a pending gate that hasn't been submitted
   743	if [ -f ".dw-state.json" ]; then
   744	  PHASE=$(jq -r '.current_phase' .dw-state.json 2>/dev/null)
   745	  case "$PHASE" in
   746	    validate|review|pr-review)
   747	      echo "You appear to be at gate $PHASE but haven't messaged the lead with proof. Send your gate proof before going idle." >&2
   748	      exit 2
   749	      ;;
   750	  esac
   751	fi
   752	
   753	exit 0
   754	```
   755	
   756	## Why Agent Team Is the Only Model (v7)
   757	
   758	Self-gating (same Claude implements AND gates) was removed in v7 because it led to
   759	rationalized step-skipping. March 26, 2026: 1,591 LOC merged with zero review.
   760	
   761	| Aspect | Agent Team (v7) |
   762	|--------|----------------|
   763	| Gate enforcement | Codex-enforced, lead validates |
   764	| Step skipping | Impossible — Skill() calls trigger hooks |
   765	| Hook enforcement | Yes (same hooks as lead) |
   766	| Review quality | Teammate Codex + lead Codex (dual) |
   767	| Context | Full independent window per teammate |
   768	
   769	## Anti-Patterns
   770	
   771	| Bad | Good |
   772	|-----|------|
   773	| Lead writes implementation code | Lead only gates and coordinates |
   774	| Teammate proceeds without gate approval | Teammate STOPS and waits at every gate |
   775	| Teammate merges its own PR | Only the lead merges |
   776	| Teammate runs Codex review | Teammates stop at dw-deliver + PR creation. Lead runs sole Codex review. dw-pr-review is lead-only. |
   777	| Teammate missing execution_context in state | Always write execution_context: "teammate" at state bootstrap. Both path + state signals needed. |
   778	| Skipping evidence in gate messages | Every gate message includes specific proof |
   779	| One teammate per ticket for 14 tickets | 2-3 teammates claiming tasks from shared list |
   780	| Lead rubber-stamps gates | Lead actually reads the proof and pushes back |
   781	| Teammate creates worktree in main repo dir | Use /tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/ for isolation |
   782	| Spawning all teammates simultaneously | Stagger by 30s (OAuth race condition) |
   783	| Spawning 4+ teammates in a wave | Max 3 concurrent (OAuth race condition) |
   784	| Using Explore subagent as investigator | Use **general-purpose** — Explore is read-only, can't SendMessage back |
   785	| Running `codex review` from main repo | Run from the **worktree** where the feature branch is checked out |
   786	| Running `gh pr merge` before removing worktree | Remove worktree first — branch-in-use blocks `--delete-branch` |
   787	| Assuming teammate's `.dw-state.json` is visible to hooks | Copy state file to main repo at PR gate (see State File Handoff) |
   788	| Leaving `.dw-state.json` in main repo after merge | Clean up state file — stale files block the next ticket |
   789	| **Using `Agent` tool with raw prompts for implementation** | **Use TeamCreate with the teammate template — `Agent(mode="bypassPermissions")` disables ALL hooks** |
   790	| **Loading dw-agent-team skill then not following it** | **If you loaded it, FOLLOW it. Loading and ignoring is worse than not loading.** |
   791	
   792	## Rationalization Red Flags
   793	
   794	<CRITICAL>
   795	If you catch yourself thinking ANY of these, you are about to bypass the protocol.
   796	STOP. Re-read the teammate template. Use it exactly.
   797	
   798	| Thought | Reality |
   799	|---------|---------|
   800	| "We're burning tokens, speed matters" | The system exists because speed without gates produces thousands of LOC of unreviewed code. March 26: 1,591 LOC, zero review. |
   801	| "I'll use Agent instead of TeamCreate, same thing" | Agent bypasses all hooks. TeamCreate preserves them. They are NOT the same. Hook-enforced since March 26. |
   802	| "These are simple tickets, skip the gates" | Simple tickets that skip gates produce the same unreviewed code as complex ones. Gates aren't proportional to complexity — they're always-on. |
   803	| "I already loaded the skill, I know what it says" | Loading ≠ following. The March 26 session loaded both skills, acknowledged the protocols, then bypassed them entirely. |
   804	| "I'll add review steps to the prompt instead" | Embedding review instructions in raw prompts is NOT the same as Skill() calls that trigger hooks. The hooks are the enforcement, not the instructions. |
   805	| "The user said to move fast / just do it" | No user instruction overrides separation of duties. Offer implement-fast for single-ticket speed. Agent teams are for quality at scale. |
   806	| "Raw prompts are more efficient" | Efficient at producing unreviewed code. The 30 minutes saved spawning is lost 10x fixing unreviewed bugs. |
   807	</CRITICAL>
   808	
   809	## Token Expiry Recovery
   810	
   811	> **Upstream bug:** Claude Code OAuth token refresh race condition (#37520).
   812	> Remove this section when Anthropic fixes the single-use refresh token locking.
   813	
   814	**Symptom:** "Not logged in - Please run /login" on lead or teammate session.
   815	The auth is NOT actually broken — new terminals work immediately.
   816	
   817	**Lead session recovery:**
   818	1. Run `/login` to re-authenticate, OR
   819	2. Start a new terminal and resume the lead role (read `.dw-state.json` + task list)
   820	
   821	**Teammate session recovery:**
   822	1. The teammate's worktree and branch are intact — no code is lost
   823	2. **Clear the watchdog ownership marker AND refresh the spawn marker BEFORE spawning replacement (REQUIRED):**
   824	   ```bash
   825	   WORKTREE="/tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/<date>/<TICKET-ID>"
   826	   rm -f "$WORKTREE/.agent-running"
   827	   printf '%s|%s\n' "$(date +%s)" "${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID:-}" > "$WORKTREE/.agent-spawned"
   828	   ```
   829	   Clearing `.agent-running` allows the replacement session to enroll on its first heartbeat.
   830	   Refreshing `.agent-spawned` resets the never-started dedup clock — if the replacement also
   831	   freezes before its first heartbeat, the watchdog can fire a new alert. Without refreshing
   832	   the marker, the stale `.frozen` mtime remains `>= SPAWN_TIME` and all subsequent alerts
   833	   for this worktree are suppressed.
   834	   The replacement's first heartbeat will also clear the `.frozen` marker written by the watchdog.
   835	3. Lead spawns a replacement teammate pointed at the same worktree/branch:
   836	   ```
   837	   Resume work on TICKET-ID. Worktree at /tmp/dev-workflow-worktrees/TICKET-ID,
   838	   branch feature/TICKET-ID. Pick up where the previous teammate left off —
   839	   check .dw-state.json and git log for progress. Follow dw-agent-team protocol.
   840	   ```
   841	4. The replacement teammate reads existing state and continues from the last completed phase
   842	
   843	**Prevention:** The 30-second stagger between spawns and max-3 cap prevent most occurrences.
   844	If you still hit this, it likely means a background token refresh coincided with a spawn.


</details>

<details><summary>Thinking</summary>

The user said "go" — they want me to pick up the next ticket and start the dev-workflow. I've read the skills. Now I need to:

1. Reset .dw-state.json for PRJ-879
2. Set hook marker
3. Create worktree
4. Spawn a teammate to implement

Let me do the setup steps. The ticket is PRJ-879 — Live items snapshot in folder browse. Blast radius: low (single component, mirrors existing pattern, ≤3 files). Path: fast.

First, let me set up the state file and hook marker, create the worktree, then spawn the teammate.

</details>

#### Tool Call: Shell (`cd…`)
<!-- call_id: tool_NIOxs4YjwndYRnBIlq4qFaLo -->

// Route guards consumed by the router. Two flavors:
//
//   <RequireAuth>{children}</RequireAuth>
//     Renders children only when the user is signed in. Unauthenticated →

// Firestore schema — single source of truth for collection shapes.
//
// Collections (flat, top-level):
//   /folders/{folderId}          — tree nodes
//   /items/{itemId}              — fabric rolls; itemId == Firestore auto-ID == QR payload, IMMUTABLE
//   /movements/{movementId}      — append-only audit log
//   /deletedRecords/{itemId}     — tombstone for 7-day restore + Firestore TTL purge
//
// Schema is locked in `research/synthesis.md` §1 (lines 37-103). Field names,
// types, and ordering follow that spec verbatim — drift here silently
// mismatches Security Rules (PRJ-805) and the Firestore writes in PRJ-780+.

// boundary in PRJ-780, not here.
//
